The Celestial Sphere is Neither Heavy Nor Light
Author proves the celestial sphere is neither heavy nor light.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the celestial sphere (al-muhaddid) is neither heavy nor light, based on the nature of its circular motion and the incompatibility of rectilinear and circular inclinations.

Core Idea
Circular motion proves no rectilinear inclination, so the celestial sphere is neither heavy nor light.

This passage presents a key argument in Islamic cosmology: the celestial spheres are neither heavy nor light because they move in circles, not straight lines. The author first gives a proof specific to the outer sphere, then a general proof based on observed circular motion. He also addresses an objection about compound motions like rolling.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the literal translation. Notice the flow from specific proof to general proof, then to the objection and response.
The last sentence in the source is incomplete due to OCR; focus on the complete argument.
2
Understand key terms
Familiarize yourself with the terms: خفة (lightness), ثقل (heaviness), ميل (inclination), استقامة (rectilinear), استدارة (circular), جهة (direction), مبدأ (principle). These are central to the argument.
Heaviness and lightness are defined as principles of rectilinear motion.
3
Analyze the specific proof
Identify why the outer sphere (al-muhaddid) is neither heavy nor light: if it had either, rectilinear motion would be possible, which requires a prior direction, but the sphere itself determines direction.
This proof only applies to the outermost sphere.
4
Analyze the general proof
Understand the general proof: all celestial spheres move circularly (proven by observation), so they have a circular inclination, not a rectilinear one. Rectilinear and circular inclinations are incompatible.
The general proof covers all celestial spheres.
5
Examine the objection and response
Consider the objection that rectilinear and circular motions can combine (e.g., rolling). The author responds that circular motion does not actively divert from direction, it just does not necessitate it. Even if inclinations conflict, their principles (cause vs. effect) may not.
The example of a thrown stone shows two opposite inclinations can coexist.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنها أنه ( أعني المحدد ) لا ثقيل ولا خفيف، لأنهما ( أي الخفة والثقل ) مبدأ الميل الصاعد والهابط، أو نفس هذين الميلين على اختلاف التفسيرين، وهما يصححان حركة محلهما بالاستقامة؛ فيقتضي وجود الثقل أو في المحدد جواز الحركة المستقيمة عليه، وذلك يستلزم تحدد الجهة قبله لا به. وهذا الدليل لابتنائه على تحديد الجهة يختص بالمحدد ولا يعم الأفلاك الباقية. والحجة العامة للكل أنها متحركة بالاستدارة بدلالة الأرصاد، ففيها مبدأ ميل مستدير بل ميل مستدير أيضاً، لأنه المقتضى القريب للحركة المستديرة، فلا يكون فيهما مبدأ ميل مستقيم لتنافيهما، أي تنافي المبدأين باعتبار تنافي الميلين، لأن الميل المستقيم يقتضي توجه الجسم إلى جهة، والمستدير يقتضي صرفه عنها. وقد يمنع التنافي بين الميلين، إذ قد يجتمعان في جسم واحد، ويحصل باجتماعهما فيه حركة مركبة كالدحرجة في الكرة، وكما في العجلة فإنها تتحرك على الاستقامة والاستدارة معاً. وليست حركة الاستدارة صارفة عن الجهة، بل هي غير مقتضية للتوجه إليها. وإن سلم التنافي بين الميلين، فلا تنافي بين المبدأين ولا بين أحدهما ومبدأ الآخر، فإن الحجر المرمي إلى فوق فيه مبدأ من الميل الهابط مع الميل الصاعد، ومبدؤه كما.
And among them is that it (i.e., the determining sphere) is neither heavy nor light, because they (i.e., lightness and heaviness) are the principle of upward and downward inclination, or they themselves are these two inclinations according to the difference of interpretations. And they set in motion their place in a straight line; so it necessitates the existence of heaviness or in the determining sphere the possibility of rectilinear motion upon it, and that entails the determination of direction before it, not by it. And this proof, due to its being based on the determination of direction, is specific to the determining sphere and does not apply to the remaining spheres. And the general proof for all is that they are in circular motion as indicated by observations, so in them is a principle of circular inclination, rather a circular inclination, because it is the proximate cause of circular motion; so there is no principle of rectilinear inclination in them due to their mutual incompatibility, i.e., the incompatibility of the two principles considering the incompatibility of the two inclinations, because rectilinear inclination necessitates directing the body to a direction, and circular inclination requires diverting it from it. And it may be objected that there is no incompatibility between the two inclinations, for they may combine in one body, and by their combination a compound motion results, like rolling in a ball, and like in a wheel, for it moves in straight and circular together. And circular motion is not a diversion from direction; rather it does not necessitate direction towards it. And if the incompatibility between the inclinations is conceded, there is no incompatibility between the principles nor between one of them and the principle of the other, for the stone thrown upward contains a principle of downward inclination with the upward inclination, and its principle is as... (incomplete).
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage contains the proof that the celestial sphere (al-muhaddid) is neither heavy nor light. The author first explains that heaviness and lightness are principles of rectilinear motion. If the sphere had heaviness or lightness, it would require a direction for straight motion, which implies a prior determination of direction, but the sphere itself determines direction. This proof is specific to the outer sphere. A general proof for all celestial spheres is that their observed circular motion indicates a circular inclination, which is incompatible with a rectilinear inclination. The author then addresses an objection: that rectilinear and circular inclinations may combine, as in rolling. The response is that circular motion does not actively divert from direction; it simply does not necessitate direction. Even if the inclinations are incompatible, the principles themselves are not incompatible, as seen in the example of a stone thrown upward which has both upward and downward inclinations simultaneously.

Key Terms
خفة

ميل

استدارة
جهة
مبدأ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that celestial spheres, because they move, must have both rectilinear and circular inclinations, similar to earthly objects rolling.
Correction: The author argues that circular motion precludes rectilinear inclination; they are incompatible. Even if compound motions exist, the celestial spheres' observed continuous circular motion indicates only a circular inclination.

Checkpoint
Why does the author say the general proof for all celestial spheres is based on observation?
A) Because we can see they are transparent.
B) Because astronomical observations show they move in circles.
C) Because they are far away.
D) Because they have no weight.

Key Takeaway
The celestial sphere is neither heavy nor light because its circular motion arises from a circular inclination, which is incompatible with the rectilinear inclination that defines heaviness and lightness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In this lesson, you learned that the celestial spheres have a single, focused circular inclination that keeps them in perfect motion without needing rectilinear pulls. Consider your own life: Are there competing inclinations—worldly desires and spiritual duties—that pull you in different directions? How can you cultivate a single, dominant inclination toward Allah that governs your movement, just as the spheres follow their circular path?
?
The author addresses an objection that two inclinations can combine, like in a rolling ball. He responds that circular motion does not actively divert one from direction; it merely does not necessitate direction. Reflect on your acts of worship: Are they merely 'non-diverting' — i.e., they keep you from sin but do not actively orient you toward Allah? Or do they create a genuine inclination that draws you closer to Him? What would it take to turn your 'non-diverting' motions into an active, orienting inclination?
?
The proof that the celestial sphere is neither heavy nor light relies on the idea that its circular motion is self-sufficient and does not require external direction. How does this reality about the heavens challenge you to examine your own dependence? Are you relying on external 'directions' (people, status, wealth) to move through life, or have you developed an internal principle that guides you independently toward your purpose? What would it mean for you to be like the celestial sphere—moved by your own intrinsic inclination toward Allah, not by external forces?

Ibn Sina's Correlation Argument: Heaviness and Coldness
Ibn Sina's correlation argument and an objector's challenge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ibn Sina's correlation argument that celestial spheres are neither hot nor cold because they lack heaviness and lightness, and the objection that this correlation only holds in the elemental realm.

Core Idea
Correlation in elements does not guarantee correlation in celestial matter.

Ibn Sina begins by arguing that heaviness always accompanies coldness and lightness always accompanies heat. Since celestial spheres are neither heavy nor light, they must be neither cold nor hot. But is this correlation universal? An objector raises a crucial point: the correlation may be limited to the elemental world. Let's examine the argument and its challenge.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Carefully read the Arabic text and its literal translation. Notice how Ibn Sina states the correlations and the conclusion.
The text mentions a textual variant where 'dryness' appears instead of 'heat'.
2
Identify Ibn Sina's reasoning
Identify the two correlations: heaviness with cold, lightness with heat. Understand why the absence of heaviness and lightness implies absence of cold and heat.
3
Understand the objection
The objector denies the correlation is absolute, restricting it to the four elements. Ask yourself: why might the celestial realm be different?
This objection sets up the need for a stronger argument.
4
Reflect on the teaching
Consider the principle: what holds true in one domain may not hold in another. This is a key methodological point in kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
( ومنها أن ( أي المحدد، وكذا غيره الأفلاك ) لا حار ولا بارد قال ابن سينا ) وذلك ( لتلازم الثقل مع البرودة ) فإن المادة إذا اشتد بردها ثقلت وإذا ثقلت بردت (و) تلازم (الخفة مع الحرارة ) فإن المادة إذا أمعن فيها التسخين خفت وإذا خفت سخنت فحيث لا ثقل ولا خفة فلا برودة ولا حرارة، وقد وقع في بعض النسخ لفظ اليبوسة بدل الحرارة، وهو سهو من القلم ) ولمانع أن يمنع التلازم بين الثقل والبرودة وبين الخفة والحرارة ( مطلقاً بل ) ذلك التلازم ) في العناصر فقط دون الأفلاك، فجاز أن يكون فيها حرارة أو برودة بلا خفة وثقل ( فإن قال : ( ابن سينا ( الحرارة علة الخفة كما أن البرودة علة الثقل ( فيمتنع التخلف ( فلو وجدنا في الأفلاك لترتب المعلولان عليهما ( قلنا : قد يتخلف الأثر عن العلة الفاعلية لعدم القابل كالحركة فإنها توجب الحرارة في العناصر القابلة لها ) والأفلاك متحركة وغير حارة لأن مادتها غير قابلة للحرارة عندكم فيجوز أن تتخلف الخفة والثقل عن الحرارة والبرودة، لأن مادة الفلك لا تقبلهما، وإن كانتا مقتضيتين لهما . ( وقال الإمام الرازي ) في المباحث المشرقية : المعتمد في أن الفلك ليس بحار ولا بارد أن يقال : ( لو كانت هي ( أي الأفلاك ( حارة لكانت في غاية الحرارة لوجود الفاعل ) الذي هو طبيعة الفلك ( والقابل ) الذي هو غير عائق ) هناك لكونها بسيطة ) والتالي باطل وإلا كان الأقرب ) من الفلك ( أسخن كرؤوس الجبال الشامخة ولاستحالة ) أي التالي باطل لما ذكر ولاستحالة ( أن تسخن الشمس وحدها حال طلوعها ( دون السماوات ( التي هي في غاية الحرارة ( مع أنها ) أعني السماوات ( أضعاف أضعافها إذ هي فيها كقطرة في بحر لجي . ( قلنا : ) في الجواب عن هذا المعتمد ( مراتب السخونة مختلفة بالنوع فربما لا تقبل مادة الفلك إلا مرتبة ) ما ( ضعيفة ) من الحرارة فلا تؤثر حرارته في عالمنا هذا ( ثم ) إن سلمنا قوة ) حرارتها ( قلنا : ( أثر التسخين ) منها ( قد لا يصل إلينا ) لأن الطبقة الزمهريرية مانعة له ( وهو ) أي الدليل المذكور ( منقوض بتسخين الشمس ) فإنها حارة يصل أثر تسخينها إلى العناصر كما اعترف المستدل به مع أن الأقرب منها ليس أسخن، ثم اعترض المصنف على المعتمد اعتراضاً رابعاً ، وهو قوله : ( والقياس عليها ) أي قياس ( مادته ( من ...
(And among them is that it (i.e., the determining sphere) and likewise the other spheres are neither hot nor cold. Ibn Sina said: That is because of the correlation of heaviness with coldness — for when matter becomes intensely cold, it becomes heavy, and when it becomes heavy, it becomes cold — and the correlation of lightness with heat — for when matter is heated thoroughly, it becomes light, and when it becomes light, it becomes hot. So where there is no heaviness and no lightness, there is no coldness and no heat. (And it occurred in some copies the word 'dryness' instead of 'heat', and that is a slip of the pen.) And an objector may deny the correlation between heaviness and coldness and between lightness and heat absolutely, rather that correlation is only in the elements, not in the celestial spheres; so it is possible that they have heat or coldness without lightness and heaviness. (If Ibn Sina says: Heat is the cause of lightness just as coldness is the cause of heaviness, so it is impossible for them to be absent; if we find them in the celestial spheres, the effects would be ordered upon them.) We say: The effect may fail to follow from the efficient cause due to the lack of a receptive subject, like motion, for it causes heat in the elements that are receptive to it, while the celestial spheres move and are not hot because their matter is not receptive to heat according to you. So it is possible that lightness and heaviness fall short of heat and coldness, because the matter of the celestial sphere does not accept them, even if they are necessitating them. (And Imam al-Razi said in al-Mabāhith al-Mashriqiyya: The reliable proof that the celestial sphere is not hot or cold is to say: If they (i.e., the spheres) were hot, they would be extremely hot due to the existence of the agent, which is the nature of the sphere, and the recipient, which is not obstructive there because they are simple. And the consequent is false; otherwise, the nearest (part of the sphere) would be hottest like the peaks of high mountains, and it is impossible that the sun alone heats at its rising without the celestial spheres that are extremely hot, even though they are many multiples of it, as a drop in a vast sea.) (We say in answer to this reliable proof:) Degrees of heat differ in kind; perhaps the matter of the sphere accepts only a weak degree of heat, so its heat does not affect our world. (Then) if we concede the strength of its heat, we say: The effect of its heating may not reach us because the frigid zone prevents it. (And) this proof (is refuted by the heating of the sun), for it is hot and its heating effect reaches the elements, as the user of the proof admits, while the nearest part of it is not hottest. Then the author objected to the reliable proof with a fourth objection, namely his saying: (and analogy upon it) i.e., analogy of its matter from... (incomplete).
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage presents the arguments and refutations regarding whether the celestial spheres are hot or cold. Ibn Sina argues by correlation: heaviness correlates with cold, lightness with heat; since spheres are neither heavy nor light, they are neither hot nor cold. An objector denies the correlation holds in the celestial domain. Ibn Sina then argues causal necessity: heat causes lightness, cold causes heaviness. The response is that the effect may fail due to lack of receptivity; celestial matter may not accept lightness/heaviness even if heat/cold are present. Then Imam al-Razi offers a proof: if spheres were hot, they would be extremely hot due to perfect agent and recipient, but then the nearest parts would be hottest like mountain peaks, and the sun alone could not heat while the vast spheres are even hotter. The response: heat degrees differ, maybe spheres accept only weak heat, or the heat may not reach us due to the frigid zone. The proof is also refuted by the sun example: the sun is hot and heats us but its nearest part is not hottest. The passage ends with mention of a fourth objection by the author, which is incomplete.

Key Terms
حرارة
برودة
ثقل
خفة
عناصر
فلك

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that if heat causes lightness, any hot object must be light.
Correction: The effect depends on the receptive subject; celestial matter may receive heat without becoming light.

Checkpoint
What is the objector's main point against Ibn Sina's correlation argument?
A) The correlation is reversed in the celestial realm.
B) The correlation only holds in the four elements, not in the celestial spheres.
C) Heaviness and lightness are not related to heat and cold.
D) The celestial spheres are not matter.

Key Takeaway
Correlations observed in the elemental world may not apply to the celestial realm due to differences in matter.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever assumed a pattern or principle you observed in one area of your life applied universally, only to later discover it didn't? What was that experience like, and how did it change your approach to forming beliefs?
?
The passage shows that even a true cause may not produce its effect if the subject is not receptive. In your relationship with Allah, what might be blocking the 'effects' of your worship or du'a—such as humility, closeness, or guidance—from manifesting in your heart? What will you do this week to become more receptive?
?
Ibn Sina's objector challenges a seemingly obvious correlation. Is there a belief or practice you hold that you have never seriously questioned, simply because 'everyone knows it'? What would it cost you to examine it honestly?

Al-Razi's Proof and Its Refutation
Al-Razi's proof that spheres are not hot and its refutations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Razi's argument that if spheres were hot they would be extremely hot, and the refutations based on degrees of heat and obstruction.

Core Idea
Extreme heat would follow from perfect agent and recipient, but degrees and obstacles prevent it.

Imam al-Razi offers what he considers the reliable proof: if the celestial spheres were hot, they would be extremely hot due to a perfect agent (their nature) and a perfect recipient (simple matter). This would have observable consequences, like the nearest part being hottest and the sun being unable to heat alone. The author provides several refutations, including the possibility of weak heat and obstruction by the frigid zone. Let's explore this exchange.

Guided Path
1
Read al-Razi's argument
Read the Arabic text and translation of al-Razi's proof. Note the premises: if spheres are hot, they are extremely hot because agent and recipient are perfect.
Al-Razi says the consequent is false because then the nearest parts would be hottest like mountain peaks, and the sun would not be able to heat alone.
2
Understand the first refutation
The author responds that degrees of heat differ in kind. The sphere may only accept a weak degree of heat, so its heat does not affect us.
This challenges the assumption that extreme heat would necessarily affect the sublunary world.
3
Understand the second refutation
Even if the heat is strong, it may not reach us due to the frigid zone (a cold layer) that acts as a barrier.
This is a physical argument about transmission of heat.
4
Understand the third refutation (the sun analogy)
The proof is refuted by the example of the sun: it is hot and heats us, yet its nearest part is not hottest. This contradicts al-Razi's claim.
This shows that the expected effect (nearest part hottest) does not hold even in the sun.
5
Synthesize the discussion
Consider how each refutation targets a different premise or implication of al-Razi's argument.
The passage ends with a mention of a fourth objection, which is incomplete.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

( قلنا : ) في الجواب عن هذا المعتمد ( مراتب السخونة مختلفة بالنوع فربما لا تقبل مادة الفلك إلا مرتبة ) ما ( ضعيفة ) من الحرارة فلا تؤثر حرارته في عالمنا هذا ( ثم ) إن سلمنا قوة ) حرارتها ( قلنا : ( أثر التسخين ) منها ( قد لا يصل إلينا ) لأن الطبقة الزمهريرية مانعة له ( وهو ) أي الدليل المذكور ( منقوض بتسخين الشمس ) فإنها حارة يصل أثر تسخينها إلى العناصر كما اعترف المستدل به مع أن الأقرب منها ليس أسخن، ثم اعترض المصنف على المعتمد اعتراضاً رابعاً ، وهو قوله : ( والقياس عليها ) أي قياس ( مادته ( من ...
(And among them is that it (i.e., the determining sphere) and likewise the other spheres are neither hot nor cold. Ibn Sina said: That is because of the correlation of heaviness with coldness — for when matter becomes intensely cold, it becomes heavy, and when it becomes heavy, it becomes cold — and the correlation of lightness with heat — for when matter is heated thoroughly, it becomes light, and when it becomes light, it becomes hot. So where there is no heaviness and no lightness, there is no coldness and no heat. (And it occurred in some copies the word 'dryness' instead of 'heat', and that is a slip of the pen.) And an objector may deny the correlation between heaviness and coldness and between lightness and heat absolutely, rather that correlation is only in the elements, not in the celestial spheres; so it is possible that they have heat or coldness without lightness and heaviness. (If Ibn Sina says: Heat is the cause of lightness just as coldness is the cause of heaviness, so it is impossible for them to be absent; if we find them in the celestial spheres, the effects would be ordered upon them.) We say: The effect may fail to follow from the efficient cause due to the lack of a receptive subject, like motion, for it causes heat in the elements that are receptive to it, while the celestial spheres move and are not hot because their matter is not receptive to heat according to you. So it is possible that lightness and heaviness fall short of heat and coldness, because the matter of the celestial sphere does not accept them, even if they are necessitating them. (And Imam al-Razi said in al-Mabāhith al-Mashriqiyya: The reliable proof that the celestial sphere is not hot or cold is to say: If they (i.e., the spheres) were hot, they would be extremely hot due to the existence of the agent, which is the nature of the sphere, and the recipient, which is not obstructive there because they are simple. And the consequent is false; otherwise, the nearest (part of the sphere) would be hottest like the peaks of high mountains, and it is impossible that the sun alone heats at its rising without the celestial spheres that are extremely hot, even though they are many multiples of it, as a drop in a vast sea.) (We say in answer to this reliable proof:) Degrees of heat differ in kind; perhaps the matter of the sphere accepts only a weak degree of heat, so its heat does not affect our world. (Then) if we concede the strength of its heat, we say: The effect of its heating may not reach us because the frigid zone prevents it. (And) this proof (is refuted by the heating of the sun), for it is hot and its heating effect reaches the elements, as the user of the proof admits, while the nearest part of it is not hottest. Then the author objected to the reliable proof with a fourth objection, namely his saying: (and analogy upon it) i.e., analogy of its matter from... (incomplete).
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage presents the arguments and refutations regarding whether the celestial spheres are hot or cold. Ibn Sina argues by correlation: heaviness correlates with cold, lightness with heat; since spheres are neither heavy nor light, they are neither hot nor cold. An objector denies the correlation holds in the celestial domain. Ibn Sina then argues causal necessity: heat causes lightness, cold causes heaviness. The response is that the effect may fail due to lack of receptivity; celestial matter may not accept lightness/heaviness even if heat/cold are present. Then Imam al-Razi offers a proof: if spheres were hot, they would be extremely hot due to perfect agent and recipient, but then the nearest parts would be hottest like mountain peaks, and the sun alone could not heat while the vast spheres are even hotter. The response: heat degrees differ, maybe spheres accept only weak heat, or the heat may not reach us due to the frigid zone. The proof is also refuted by the sun example: the sun is hot and heats us but its nearest part is not hottest. The passage ends with mention of a fourth objection by the author, which is incomplete.

Key Terms
فاعل
قابل
بسيط
سخونة
زمهرير

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that if something is hot, it must be extremely hot if the agent and recipient are perfect.
Correction: Degrees of heat differ; a perfect agent may produce only weak heat if the recipient only accepts that degree.

Checkpoint
What is the second refutation of al-Razi's proof?
A) The heat may be weak.
B) The heat may be blocked by the frigid zone.
C) The sun's heat refutes the argument.
D) Celestial matter is not receptive.

Key Takeaway
Even a well-structured proof like al-Razi's can be refuted by considering degrees, obstacles, and counterexamples.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear a logical argument about Allah (like al-Razi's proof), do you accept it quickly because it seems sound, or do you pause to look for hidden assumptions and counterexamples? Which of your beliefs about God might be based on incomplete reasoning that this lesson challenges you to re-examine?
?
The sun is a counterexample that overturns a natural assumption about heat distribution. In your spiritual life, what 'sunlike' facts — clear experiences or verses — have you overlooked because they didn't fit your expectations? How can you make room for them?
?
The lesson suggests that even if the spheres are hot, their heat might not reach us due to obstacles (frigid zone). Could there be spiritual 'frigid zones' in your life — habits, sins, or distractions — that block the warmth of Allah's guidance from reaching your heart? What concrete step can you take today to remove one such barrier?

The Motion of the Fixed Stars and Its Estimated Periods
Estimates for the revolution period of the fixed stars.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the various historical estimates for the revolution period of the fixed stars and the basis for each estimate.

Core Idea
The fixed stars move, but so slowly that their motion requires long-term observation.

This passage presents the astronomical claim that the fixed stars have their own slow motion beyond the daily rotation. Several medieval astronomers proposed different periods for one complete revolution, ranging from 30,000 to 25,200 years, each based on observational data. By reading this source, you will see how early scholars used careful observation and calculation to estimate celestial motions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on motion and periods
Read the Arabic passage slowly, noting the different numerical estimates. Then read the translation to understand the arguments.
Pay attention to the sources of each estimate: Ptolemy, later scholars, Maragha.
2
Identify the four estimates
List the four periods mentioned: 30,000, 36,000, 23,760, and 25,200 years. Note which one is considered baseless and which one agrees with the new observation.
3
Understand the logical structure
The author explains that astronomers deduced the motion from observation and then calculated the full period by extrapolation. See how 'observation' and 'computation' work together.
The phrase 'فقدروا بالحساب' indicates the computational step.

قوله : ( تقطع في كل مئة سنة جزءاً واحداً فهي تقطع في كل ثلاثة آلاف سنة برجاً واحداً .
قوله : (للرصد الجديد قيل : هو الرصد الذي تولاه نصر الدين الطوسي بمراغة .
That (the fixed stars) claim that they (the fixed stars) have, despite being moved by the daily motion following the sphere of spheres, a motion specific to them (very slow) and that they complete the revolution in thirty thousand years. This statement has become famous among the common people and has no basis according to the astronomers. And it was said: they complete the revolution in thirty-six thousand years, based on the fact that Ptolemy found by observation that they cut one degree every hundred years. And it was said: they complete the revolution in twenty-three thousand seven hundred and sixty years, based on what the later scholars found, that they cut one degree every sixty-six years. And it was said: they complete it in twenty-five thousand two hundred years, based on a group of the later researchers found they cut one degree every seventy years. And this is what agrees with the new observation at Maragha. And they only ruled that they complete the revolution in the mentioned periods because they sensed from them a slow motion by observation, as you have known. And they believed that they complete the revolution due to its continuity, so they calculated by computation the completion of the rotation in this disputed period as we summarized. And they are only called (the fixed stars, excluding the seven planets) fixed either because of the slowness of their motion, so we do not sense [it] except by precise examination of their conditions known by observations between long periods. Therefore, they were hidden from the early scholars until they claimed that there are eight spheres and that the daily motion belongs to the sphere of the fixed stars.

His statement: (it cuts one degree every hundred years, then it cuts one zodiacal sign every three thousand years).
His statement: (the new observation) it is said: it is the observation undertaken by Nasir al-Din al-Tusi at Maragha.
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage presents a series of astronomical claims about the motion of the fixed stars and explains the origin of their name. The author begins by stating the central claim: the fixed stars, though participating in the daily motion, have their own very slow motion. Several estimates for the period of their complete revolution are then given: 30,000 years (a popular but baseless opinion), 36,000 years (based on Ptolemy's observation that the stars move one degree per century), 23,760 years (based on later scholars finding one degree per 66 years), and 25,200 years (based on yet another group finding one degree per 70 years, corroborated by the Maragha observatory). The author then explains that the reason they are called 'fixed' is the extreme slowness of their motion—so slow that it is imperceptible without careful observation over long intervals. This is why early astronomers mistakenly thought there were only eight spheres, attributing the daily motion entirely to the sphere of the fixed stars. The footnote clarifies the conversion of degrees to zodiacal signs and identifies the 'new observation' as the one undertaken by Nasir al-Din al-Tusi at Maragha.

الحركة اليومية
فلك الأفلاك
الدورة
الرصد
بطليموس
مراغة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The fixed stars are completely stationary.
Correction: They do move, but very slowly.

Checkpoint

A) 30,000 years
B) 36,000 years
C) 23,760 years
D) 25,200 years

Key Takeaway
The fixed stars have a slow proper motion, and different ancient and medieval astronomers proposed different revolution periods based on observations.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage shows multiple conflicting estimates from astronomers. Is there any belief you hold with complete certainty that might be overturned by new evidence? Are you humble enough to adjust your understanding when faced with contrary observation?
?
Ptolemy, a great authority, calculated 36,000 years; later scholars found different numbers. Does this challenge your trust in scholarly authority? How do you balance respect for predecessors with the duty to seek truth yourself, especially in matters of faith?
?
The common people held a 30,000-year cycle with no basis. Are there beliefs in your own religious community that are widely accepted but lack solid foundation? Will you investigate them or remain passive?

Why Fixed Stars Are Called Fixed
Explanation of the term 'fixed stars' and clarification of their motion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the reason why the fixed stars are called 'fixed' and the historical confusion surrounding their motion.

Core Idea
The stars are called fixed because their motion is too slow to be noticed without careful observation.

This passage explains the linguistic and astronomical reasoning behind the term 'fixed stars'. Despite their name, these stars do move, but their motion is so slow that early astronomers did not detect it, leading to a mistaken model of eight spheres. The source also provides a clarifying note on the conversion of degrees to zodiacal signs and identifies the Maragha observatory as the source of the 'new observation'.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on naming and the footnote
Read the Arabic passage that explains why the stars are called fixed, then read the translation and the notes.
Notice the phrase 'إما لبطء حركتها فلا نحس' as the core reason.
2
Analyze the reasoning
The author gives two alternative reasons using 'إما' (either). Identify both: slowness of motion, and the need for precise observation over long periods.
3
Understand the historical context
Early scholars missed this motion, leading to an incorrect model. The footnote clarifies the 'new observation' as that of Nasir al-Din al-Tusi at Maragha.
This connects to the previous lesson's estimates.

The Sun's Motion: Eccentric vs. Epicycle
Defines eccentric and epicycle models and explains the sun's single inequality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the difference between the eccentric and epicycle models in explaining the sun's single inequality, and why the eccentric requires fewer motions.

Core Idea
The eccentric model explains the sun's speed variation with one motion; the epicycle needs two.

This passage from al-Isfahani's commentary contrasts two astronomical models for the sun's apparent motion. It explains why the eccentric model is simpler for the sun's single inequality, addresses an objection about the apogee, and then shows how the sun's speed variation is constant and how the epicycle must be constrained to match.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First read the Arabic and then the English to get the flow of the argument. Notice the technical terms.
The passage uses a concise style typical of kalam texts.
2
Identify the two models
Find where the eccentric and epicycle are defined and how many motions each requires for the sun's inequality.
The eccentric is completed by one motion, the epicycle by two.
3
Understand the objection and response
Notice the objection about the apogee motion and the author's clarification that only speed variation is considered, not the apogee's motion.
The objection seems to argue both models need two motions, but the author distinguishes the apogee motion.
4
Study the sun's inequality
Read the description of the sun being slow in the northern signs and fast in the southern signs, and how each model explains this.
The eccentric explains it naturally by placing the apogee in the north.
5
Review the epicycle constraints
See the additional restrictions needed for the epicycle to produce the same effect: synchronous period and matching radius.
These constraints make the epicycle more complex for the sun.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المرصد الأول - الفصل الثاني : القسم الأول : المقصد الرابع : فلك الشمس
يكفيهما حركة الخارج. فلذلك قالوا : أصل الخارج المركز يتم بحركة واحدة وأصل التدوير يتم بحركتين. فإن قلت لا بد لتحريك أوجها من حركة أخرى، وهي حركة ممثلها فيكون لها على أصل الخارج أيضاً حركتان . قلت : كلامنا في مجرد السرعة والبطء ولا حاجة لهما إلى حركة أخرى، وأيضاً إذا اعتبر تحريك الأوج فلا بد في أصل التدوير من حركة ثالثة مستندة إلى تحريك فلك البروج كما ذكروه ( و ) للشمس (اختلاف واحد هو سرعته في نصف من فلكه بل في نصف بعينه من فلك البروج ) وبطؤه في نصف ) آخر ( بعينه لا يتغير ذلك ) بل هي أبداً بطيئة في البروج الشمالية وسريعة في الجنوبية وذلك ظاهر على أصل الخارج بأن يكون الأوج في البروج الشمالية فتكون الشمس هناك أبعد من الأرض وأبطأ حركة وفيما يقابلها أقرب وأسرع . وإذا أريد الإبطاء والإسراع على هذا الوجه بعينه من أصل التدوير احتيج إلى قيود أشار إليها بقوله : ( فلنفرض التدوير بحيث يتم دوره مع دورة حامله و) بحيث يكون (قطره) بل نصف قطره ) بقدر بعد مركز الخارج عن مركز العالم ولا بد
The First Observatory - Chapter Two: First Section: Fourth Objective: The Sphere of the Sun
The motion of the eccentric suffices for both. Therefore they said: The eccentric (al-kharij al-markaz) is completed by one motion, and the epicycle (al-tadwir) is completed by two motions. If you say: There must be another motion to move its apogee, which is the motion of its representative, so it would have two motions on the eccentric as well. I say: Our discussion is about mere speed and slowness, and they have no need for another motion. Also, if moving the apogee is considered, then in the epicycle there must be a third motion dependent on the motion of the sphere of the zodiac (falak al-buruj) as they mentioned. And for the sun there is a single inequality: its speed in half of its sphere, rather in a specific half of the sphere of the zodiac, and its slowness in another specific half, and this does not change. Rather it is always slow in the northern signs and fast in the southern ones. That is apparent on the eccentric model by having the apogee in the northern signs, so the sun is farther from the earth and slower, and in the opposite it is closer and faster. And if one intends the slowing and speeding in this exact manner from the epicycle model, one needs restrictions which he indicated by his saying: Let us assume the epicycle such that its period is completed with the period of its deferent, and such that its diameter, rather its radius, equals the distance of the center of the eccentric from the center of the world — and it must be...
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage defines and contrasts two astronomical models for explaining the sun's apparent motion: the eccentric (al-kharij al-markaz) and the epicycle (al-tadwir). It begins by stating that for explaining the sun's single inequality (difference in speed), the eccentric model suffices with one motion, whereas the epicycle model requires two motions. An objection is raised: the eccentric also needs an additional motion to move the apogee (the point farthest from Earth), so it too requires two motions. The answer clarifies that the discussion concerns only the speed variation (acceleration and deceleration), not the motion of the apogee; the apogee's motion is separate. Moreover, if one insists on including the apogee's motion, then the epicycle would need a third motion dependent on the sphere of the zodiac. The passage then explains the sun's single inequality: it is slow in the northern half of the zodiac and fast in the southern half, which is constant. This is naturally explained by the eccentric model by placing the apogee in the north, making the sun farther and slower there. For the epicycle to produce the same effect, additional constraints are necessary, such as matching the epicycle's radius to the eccentric's center offset and synchronizing its period with the deferent.

Key Terms
الخارج المركز
التدوير
الأوج
فلك البروج
الاختلاف الواحد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The eccentric model is simpler because it uses only one motion, but it still requires a motion for the apogee, making it not simpler.
Correction: The passage clarifies that the apogee motion is separate from the speed variation; the eccentric model explains the speed variation with a single motion.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how many motions does the eccentric model require to account for the sun's single inequality?
A) One motion
B) Two motions
C) Three motions
D) No motion

Key Takeaway
The eccentric model requires one motion to explain the sun's speed variation, while the epicycle requires two motions and additional constraints to produce the same effect.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The eccentric model explains the sun's speed with a single motion. Is there one core intention (niyyah) in your life that drives your actions, or do you rely on multiple 'epicycles' to justify inconsistencies? Will you commit to identifying that one intention today and align your actions with it?
?
The sun's pattern of slowness in the north and speed in the south is constant and never changes. What 'northern sign' in your spiritual practice — a prayer, a charity, a habit — is consistently weak? Can you shift your 'apogee' so that you draw nearer to Allah in that area, starting this week?
?
The author distinguishes between the motion for speed variation and the motion of the apogee. What distractions or secondary concerns do you mistake for the core of your faith? Are you willing to strip away those distractions and focus on what truly determines your spiritual speed?

Why the Moon Must Be on an Epicycle
Proof that the moon's speed variation across the entire zodiac requires an epicycle.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the moon's observed speed variation across the entire zodiac leads astronomers to conclude it moves on an epicycle.

Core Idea
The moon's speed varies everywhere; that forces an epicycle model.

In this passage, al-Iji presents the fifth objective on lunar spheres. He begins by contrasting the moon's motion with the sun's: the sun only speeds up and slows down in specific halves of the zodiac, but the moon does so everywhere. This observed difference is the key evidence that the moon must be on an epicycle rather than a simple concentric sphere.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once and then its English translation. Pay attention to the contrast between the sun and the moon.
2
Identify the key observation
Notice that the passage says the moon speeds up and slows down 'in all parts of the sphere of the zodiac' (في جميع فلك البروج). This is different from the sun's behavior.
This uniform variation is the crucial clue.
3
Connect observation to conclusion
Understand why this observation forces the moon to be on an epicycle: the epicycle's shorter period causes speed changes everywhere, unlike a simple deferent.
The conclusion is that the moon is on an epicycle whose period is less than its deferent's.

Concerning the spheres of the moon, since the moon follows the sun in fame and illumination after it, and it is found not like the sun: the sun speeds up in a specific half of the sphere of the zodiac and slows down in another half, but the moon is not like that. Commentary
This passage proves that the moon's motion requires an epicycle model. It first contrasts the moon with the sun: the sun has a fixed pattern of speeding up in one half of the zodiac and slowing in the other, but the moon's speed varies throughout the entire zodiac without restriction. From this observed difference, it is concluded that the moon must be on an epicycle whose orbital period is shorter than that of its deferent (i.e., it completes its epicycle before completing one deferent revolution). This arrangement explains why the moon's speed changes in all zodiac sectors. The final sentence (incomplete) likely introduces how to set up the epicycle parameters.

Why the Moon's Variable Speed Requires an Epicycle
Commentator proves moon's epicycle due to non-restricted speed variation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the moon's speed variation across the entire zodiac requires an epicyclic model, and how this model differs from the sun's simple eccentric.

Core Idea
The moon's speed varies everywhere, so it cannot be a simple eccentric like the sun.

This lesson unpacks a key astronomical argument from Islamic cosmology: why the moon's motion demands a more complex model than the sun's. The sun's speed variation is confined to two halves of the zodiac, but the moon's speed changes throughout. Astronomers concluded that the moon must be on an epicycle, with refinements involving an eccentric and an inclined sphere.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage with its translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage once, then follow the literal translation. Let the technical terms settle before analyzing.
The passage is dense; don't worry about every detail on first read.
2
Contrast the sun's and moon's speed patterns
Notice the key difference: the sun speeds up and slows down only in specific halves of the zodiac, while the moon does so everywhere.
This contrast is the foundation for the epicycle argument.
3
Understand the epicycle proof and its refinement
Follow how the commentator first argues for an epicycle with a shorter period, then corrects it with a longer period, and finally adds an eccentric and inclined sphere.
The refinement is based on observational data about the moon's return to specific states.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ذلك أن نفرض حركة الحامل شبيهة بحركة الخارج في جهتها بحيث يتممان الدورتين معاً وأن نفرض حركة التدوير شبيهة بهما على وجه تكون في القطعة البعيدة إلى خلاف جهة حركة الحامل وفي القطعة القريبة إلى جهتها. المقصد الخامس: أفلاك القمر. لما كان القمر تلو الشمس في الشهرة والإنارة عقبها به وهو وجد لا كالشمس حيث تسرع الشمس في نصف بعينه من فلك البروج وتبطئ في نصف آخر منه وليس القمر كذلك بل هو يسرع ويبطئ في جميع فلك البروج لا يختص إسراعه وإبطاؤه بجزء معين منه دون آخر. فعلم بذلك أنه على تدوير يتم دوره قبل دورة حامله. فإذا فرض القمر في موضع من التدوير والتدوير في موضع من الحامل، وكان هناك للقمر بواسطة التدوير حالة مخصوصة من الإسراع والإبطاء فإذا عاد القمر إلى موضعه بحركة التدوير قبل دورة حامله عادت تلك الحالة المخصوصة إليه في جزء آخر من فلك البروج وتنتقل تلك الحالة في دورة أخرى إلى جزء ثالث منه. وهكذا. ثم إن هذا التصوير وإن كان كافياً لعدم اختصاص السرعة والبطء بأجزاء معينة من البروج إلا أنه يقتضي أن يكون عود القمر إلى الحالة المخصوصة قبل العود إلى جزء بعينه من البروج وذلك باطل لأن المعلوم بالرصد أن عوده إليها بعد العود إلى جزء بعينه من البروج بزمان قليل فالصحيح أن يقال: يتم دوره بعد دورة حامله. ثم إذا قيس سرعة إلى سرعة وبطء إلى بطء لم يكن مثله بل أسرع أو أبطأ. فعلم بذلك أن تدويره مركوز في ثخن فلك خارج المركز إذ حينئذ تكون القسي المفروضة في التدوير المتساوية في أنفسها متفاوتة في الصغر والكبر بحسب الرؤية فيقع التفاوت في الحالة العائدة مقيسة إلى نظيرتها. ثم وجد غاية سرعته في تربيعي الشمس فهو يجب أن يكون في كل واحد من تربيعيها في حضيض الخارج المقتضي لغاية السرعة والأوج يقابله ضرورة. فله فلك آخر سوى التدوير وحامله يخرج ذلك الفلك ويحرك أوجه إلى خلاف جهة حركته وهو الفلك الذي يكون الخارج المركز في ثخنه وسميناه المائل فيجتمع القمر والأوج عند المقابلة ثم يتقابلان في التربيع الثاني.
That we suppose the motion of the deferent similar to the motion of the eccentric in its direction such that they complete two revolutions together, and that we suppose the motion of the epicycle similar to them such that in the far arc it is opposite the direction of the deferent's motion and in the near arc it is in its direction. The fifth goal: The orbits of the moon. Since the moon follows the sun in fame and illumination after it, and it is not like the sun where the sun speeds up in one particular half of the zodiac and slows down in another half, but the moon is not so; rather it speeds up and slows down in all of the zodiac, its acceleration and deceleration not being restricted to a particular part without another. So it was known by that that it is on an epicycle whose period is completed before the period of its deferent. For if the moon is assumed at a place on the epicycle and the epicycle at a place on the deferent, and there is for the moon by means of the epicycle a particular state of acceleration and deceleration, then when the moon returns to its place by the motion of the epicycle before the revolution of its deferent, that particular state returns to it in another part of the zodiac, and that state transfers in another revolution to a third part of it, and so on. Then this depiction, although sufficient for the non-restriction of speed and slowness to specific parts of the zodiac, necessarily implies that the return of the moon to the particular state occurs before the return to a specific part of the zodiac, and that is false because what is known by observation is that its return to it occurs after the return to a specific part of the zodiac by a short time. So the correct thing is to say: its period is completed after the revolution of its deferent. Then if speed is compared to speed and slowness to slowness, it is not exactly like it but faster or slower. So it was known by that that its epicycle is embedded in the thickness of an eccentric sphere, for then the assumed arcs on the epicycle that are equal in themselves vary in smallness and greatness according to sight, so variation occurs in the returning state compared to its counterpart. Then its maximum speed was found at the quadratures of the sun, so it must be in each of its quadratures at the perigee of the eccentric which necessitates maximum speed, and the apogee opposite it necessarily. So it has another sphere besides the epicycle and its deferent; that sphere emerges and moves its apogee opposite to its direction of motion, and it is the sphere in whose thickness is the eccentric, and we called it the inclined one. Then the moon and the apogee meet at opposition, then they are opposite at the second quadrature.
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage is a proof that the moon moves on an epicycle and that its motion is modeled by a deferent, an epicycle, and an additional sphere. The commentator begins by explaining the sun's motion: it speeds up in one half of the zodiac and slows down in the other, which is accounted for by an eccentric sphere. The moon, however, speeds up and slows down throughout the entire zodiac, not restricted to halves. This indicates that the moon is on an epicycle whose period is shorter than that of its deferent. The commentator illustrates: if the moon starts at a specific point on the epicycle and the epicycle at a specific point on the deferent, then the moon will have a particular state of speed. When the epicycle returns to its original position before the deferent completes a revolution, that state reappears at a different zodiacal longitude. This explains non-restriction, but it would imply that the moon returns to the same state before returning to the same longitude, which contradicts observation. Observations show that the moon returns to the same state only slightly after returning to the same longitude. Hence, the correct account is that the epicycle's period is longer than the deferent's. Furthermore, when comparing speeds, they are not exactly equal but slightly different, implying that the epicycle is embedded in an eccentric sphere. The moon's greatest speed occurs at its quadratures with the sun, so the perigee must be at the quadrature and the apogee opposite. This necessitates an additional sphere that moves the apogee opposite to the direction of motion, called the inclined sphere, which contains the eccentric in its thickness. The moon and apogee meet at opposition and are opposite at the second quadrature.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The moon's speed variation follows the same pattern as the sun's, confined to two halves of the zodiac.
Correction: The passage specifically states that the moon speeds up and slows down in all parts of the zodiac, not just in halves, requiring an epicycle rather than a simple eccentric.

Checkpoint
Why does the initial epicycle model (with a shorter period) fail?
A) It does not explain the moon's acceleration and deceleration.
B) It predicts the moon returns to the same speed state before returning to the same longitude, which contradicts observation.
C) It requires an additional sphere that is not observed.
D) It only works for the sun, not the moon.

Key Takeaway
The moon's universal speed variation demands an epicycle mounted on an eccentric sphere, with an additional inclined sphere to correctly model the timing of maximum speed.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

The Three Lunar Anomalies
Enumerates three lunar anomalies and their geometric causes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three types of lunar anomalies described in classical Islamic astronomy and their proposed causes.

Core Idea
The moon's motion has three anomalies due to epicycle, eccentric, and variable radius.

In Ptolemaic astronomy, the moon's motion was modeled with epicycles and eccentrics. This passage from Sharh al-Mawaqif explains three distinct anomalies (ikhtilāfāt) that arise from these models. Understanding these anomalies is crucial for grasping how pre-modern astronomers accounted for the moon's complex motion.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to get an overview. Then read the translation to understand the descriptions of each anomaly.
The text is technical; focus on the three distinct types mentioned.
2
Identify the three anomalies
Find where the text lists the first, second, and third anomalies. Note their names: due to epicycle (التدوير), due to eccentric (الخارج), due to variable radius of epicycle (تفاوت قطر التدوير).
The second anomaly involves mean apogee/perigee.
3
Understand the geometric descriptions
For each anomaly, visualize the alignments described: the epicycle's diameter, the line through centers, and the shifting of apogee/perigee.
The commentator clarifies that the second anomaly's cause is not simply the eccentric.
4
Reflect on the unknown cause
The passage states the quiddity (māhīyah) of the second anomaly is known but its cause (limmiyyah) is not. Consider why this is a significant epistemological point.
This shows the limits of astronomical knowledge in the Ptolemaic tradition.

First observatory - Chapter Two: Section One: Fifth Objective: Lunar Spheres. This angle from the mean moon, that is, the motion of the center of its epicycle, and sometimes it is increased to obtain its equation, that is, the motion of its own center. The limit of this anomaly is half the radius of the epicycle. (And) the second is the anomaly (that occurs due to the eccentric). For when the center of the epicycle is at apogee or perigee, a specific diameter of it coincides with the line passing through the centers of the world, the eccentric, and the epicycle, and through the apogee and perigee. The upper end of this diameter is the epicycle's apogee, which is the beginning of its proper motion, and the other end is its perigee opposite it. So they are aligned in both cases with the center of the world and also the center of the eccentric. But when the center of the epicycle leaves the apogee and perigee, that diameter no longer coincides with the line from the center of the world to the center of the epicycle reaching its top, nor with the line from the center of the eccentric to that center. So the mentioned apogee and its opposite are not aligned with any of the centers of the world and the eccentric. Rather, they are always aligned with another point, as you will know. They are called the mean apogee and mean perigee, and they differ from the visible apogee and perigee away from apogee and perigee. Know that this anomaly is not due to the carrier of the epicycle being eccentric, but it is an anomaly occurring between the two apogees, the quiddity of which is known but the cause is not. (And) the third is the anomaly (that occurs due to the variation of the epicycle's diameter in greatness and smallness (in its nearness and distance due to its eccentric carrier). For if we assume that the first anomaly reaches its limit which is half the radius of the epicycle as before, then the center of the epicycle at that time is at apogee, its radius has a certain magnitude in visibility, but if it is at perigee, it has a greater magnitude than that. Similarly for the first anomaly if it is not at the limit, there also occurs variation according to nearness and distance. So this anomaly is the addition that accompanies the first anomaly, therefore it is considered a second anomaly subordinate to the first. (And) for the moon (in...). For when the epicycle is at apogee for example, the apogee must coincide with the apogee and be united with it. So if we assume a line starting from the apogee ending at... for example, then the apogee must coincide with the apogee and be united with it. Then if we assume a line starting from the apogee ending at the perigee, that line passes first through the center of the epicycle, then through its perigee, then through the center of the eccentric, then through the center of the world, and ends at the perigee. And if the center of the epicycle is at perigee, then the perigee of the eccentric and the perigee of the epicycle must be united. Then if we assume a line starting from the apogee ending at the apogee, this line passes first through the center of the epicycle, then through the perigee which have become united, then through the center of the eccentric, and ends at the apogee. His statement: 'they both' means the two mentioned ends. His statement: 'in these two cases' means the center of the epicycle being at apogee and being at perigee. His statement: 'also' is attached to the center of the world and the center of the eccentric together, i.e., the two mentioned ends are aligned with the center of the world and the center of the eccentric as they are aligned with the apogee and perigee. It is possible that it is attached to the center of the eccentric alone, i.e., they are aligned with the center of the eccentric as they are aligned with the center of the world. But the first is more appropriate. His statement: 'to its center' means the center of the epicycle. His statement: 'likewise' means reaching its top. His statement: 'to another point' means it is on the side of the perigee from the center of the world according to his choice. His statement: 'as you will know' means you will know in the upcoming notice of this objective. His statement: 'and they are called mean apogee and mean perigee' which were visible at apogee and perigee before the departure of the center of the epicycle from apogee and perigee. His statement: 'the visible' etc. means the visible after the departure of the center of the epicycle from apogee and perigee. His statement: 'and know that this anomaly' is an indication of a refutation of the author in his statement: 'the one due to the eccentric'. His statement: 'it is not due to the carrier of the epicycle being eccentric' because if it were so, then that diameter of the epicycle would always coincide with the line from the center of the eccentric to the center of the epicycle reaching its top. But the consequent is false, so then the cause of this anomaly is a composite matter of the carrier of the epicycle being
Source pages p. 123

Commentary
This passage is an astronomical exposition of three lunar anomalies as presented in the context of Ptolemaic cosmology within Sharh al-Mawaqif. The commentator begins by stating the three types of 'ikhtilāf' (diversity/anomaly) in the moon's motion. The first anomaly is due to the epicycle itself: when the moon moves on the epicycle, its center's motion relative to the mean moon varies, reaching a maximum equal to the epicycle's radius. The second anomaly is due to the eccentric (al-khārij): when the epicycle's center is at apogee or perigee, a diameter aligns with the line through the centers of the world and the eccentric, but when it moves away, the epicycle's apogee and perigee shift from alignment with these centers, instead aligning with another point called the mean apogee and mean perigee. The commentator notes that this anomaly's cause is not simply the eccentric carrier, but an unknown cause ('ulimat ānnīyatuhu wa lam tu'lam limmiyyatuhu). The third anomaly is due to the epicycle's diameter varying in size with distance from the observer, caused by the eccentric carrier: when the epicycle is at apogee, its apparent radius is smaller; at perigee, larger. This adds to the first anomaly and is thus considered a second anomaly. The commentator then engages in a detailed refutation of the author's statement, arguing that the second anomaly is not merely due to the eccentric carrier, as that would imply constant alignment, which is false. Instead, the cause is composite. The commentary uses geometric reasoning to explain the alignments and variations, emphasizing the distinction between visible and mean apogee/perigee.

Key Terms
اختلاف
التدوير
الخارج
الأوج
الحضيض
ذروة وسطى
حضيض أوسط

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The second anomaly is caused solely by the eccentric carrier.
Correction: The text explicitly states that the cause of the second anomaly is unknown; its quiddity is known but its 'limmiyyah' (cause) is not. The commentator refutes the idea that it is simply due to the eccentric carrier.

Checkpoint

A) The diameter of the epicycle
B) Half the radius of the epicycle
C) The full radius of the epicycle
D) The distance from the center of the world

Key Takeaway
The moon's motion in Ptolemaic astronomy is explained by three anomalies: from the epicycle, from the eccentric (with an unknown cause), and from the variable radius of the epicycle.

The Cycle of Planetary Motions
Describes the motion cycle of the five planets.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the sequence of motions (fast, slow, stationary, retrograde, direct) that the five wandering planets exhibit according to classical Islamic astronomy.

Core Idea
Planets go through a predictable cycle of direct motion, station, retrograde, station, and direct motion.

This passage from al-Mawaqif explains the fascinating behavior of the five planets known as 'the wandering ones' (المتحيرة). Unlike the fixed stars, these planets appear to move irregularly: they speed up, slow down, stop, and even reverse direction. The author describes this cycle in detail, setting the stage for the epicyclic model that explains these apparent motions.

Guided Path
1
Read the description of the motion cycle
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice the sequence: fast motion, slowing, stationary, retrograde, slowing, stationary, direct motion.
This cycle is observed for all five planets.
2
Identify the key terms
List the key terms: سريعة (fast), بطء (slow), وقوف (stationary), رجوع (retrograde), استقامة (direct). Memorize them.
3
Understand the universality claim
The passage states that these motions occur in all parts of the zodiac, not just specific ones. Ask yourself why this is important.
This rules out explanations based on fixed positions.
4
Connect to the epicyclic model
The passage hints that the epicycle center moves along the deferent at the same speed as the sun's motion. Reflect on how this explains the observed cycle.
This is the beginning of the causal explanation.

The Sixth Objective: The Remaining Spheres. Concerning the five remaining spheres, called the wandering (planets), they are fast in motion toward the succession of the signs, then they begin to slow, and that slowing increases until these planets stop in a part of the parts of the signs for days, then they begin to retrograde contrary to the succession, gradually each one of them in speed in its retrogradation to a certain limit, then it begins to slow in its retrogradation until it stops a second time, then it becomes direct (i.e., it moves to the succession), gradually increasing in speed in its direct motion to a limit, and that occurs for them in the parts of the zodiacal sphere. Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This passage is a descriptive definition of the characteristic motions of the five planets (Mercury, Venus, Mars, Jupiter, Saturn), known as 'the wandering' (المتحيرة). The author describes a cycle: they move fast in direct motion (from west to east), then gradually slow down, stop (stationary), then begin retrograde motion (east to west) which accelerates to a maximum, then slows down, stops again, and resumes direct motion. This pattern is not confined to specific zodiacal positions but occurs throughout the zodiac. From these observed states, it is inferred that the epicycle center of these planets moves on a deferent sphere at the same rate as the sun's mean motion, always keeping alignment with the sun. The text begins to apply this to Mercury and Venus but is cut off.

The five planets exhibit a repeating cycle of fast direct motion, slowing, station, retrograde, slowing, station, and resumption of direct motion, which occurs uniformly across the zodiac.

The Special Epicycle of Venus and Mercury
Explains planetary motions and structural difference of epicycle centers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the observed motions of Venus and Mercury differ from the outer planets, revealing that their epicycle centers are attached to the sun.

Core Idea
Venus and Mercury's epicycle centers are fixed to the sun; outer planets' are not.

This passage from al-Iji's al-Mawaqif explains the key observational evidence that distinguishes the inferior planets (Venus and Mercury) from the outer planets. By tracking their conjunctions and separations from the sun, astronomers deduced a fundamental structural difference in the Ptolemaic model. Let's follow the argument step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation, to get a sense of the argument.
2
Identify the general principle
Notice how the passage begins with a general statement about the five planets' motion relative to fixed stars, establishing that the epicycle carrier moves eastward.
3
Focus on Venus and Mercury
Observe the detailed description of Venus and Mercury's conjunctions and separations from the sun, and the maximum angular distances given.
These specific numbers are important.
4
Extract the conclusion for Venus/Mercury
The passage concludes that the center of their epicycle is attached to the sun, and their distance from the sun is due only to epicycle motion.
5
Contrast with outer planets
Read the final part about the upper planets, noting that their retrograde motion occurs at opposition, showing their epicycle centers are not sun-attached.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ذكر من أحوالها أنها في تدوير تزيد حركته في نصفه المخالف على حركة حامله كما مر في الفائدة الثانية ثم إنها أي الكواكب الخمسة تكون غريبة من الثوابت فتلحقها مقارنة إياها ثم تفارقها مخلفة لها إلى المغرب فعلم بذلك أن حامل تدويرها متحرك من المغرب إلى المشرق والزهرة وعطارد يقارنان الشمس مستقيمين ثم يتفرقان عن الشمس حتى يصيرا شرقيين عنها فيطلعان بعدها ويغربان كذلك متباعدين في هذا التفرق عنها إلى حد ما فغاية بعد الزهرة عن الشمس سبعة وأربعون جزءاً وغاية بعد عطارد عنها سبعة وعشرين جزءاً ثم يرجعان إلى خلاف التوالي متقاربين منها حتى يقارناها راجعين مقارنة ثانية ثم يغربان أي يصيران غربيين عنها فيغربان حينئذ قبلها لا بعدها كما ذكره و كذا يطلعان قبلها متباعدين في التغريب عنها إلى حد ما ثم يرجعان عن صوب الرجوع إلى سمت الاستقامة حتى يقارباها في الاستقامة كما ذكرناه أولاً فعلم بذلك أن مركز تدويرهما خاصة ملازم لمركز الشمس وأن بعدهما عنها شرقاً أو غرباً إنما هو بحركة تدويرهما فقط فالبواقي من المتحيرة وهي العلوية ليست كذلك فإن رجوعها بل أواسطه إنما تكون وهي في مقابلة الشمس فهي في الحضيض حينئذ كما أن أواسطه استقامتها إنما تكون في مقارنة الشمس إياها وهي حينئذ في الذروة
Mentioning of their states: that they are in an epicycle whose motion in its opposite half exceeds the motion of its carrier, as passed in the second benefit. Then they, i.e. the five planets, are strange from the fixed stars, so they catch up to them in conjunction, then separate from them, leaving them behind to the west. So it is known by that that the carrier of their epicycle moves from the west to the east. And Venus and Mercury are in conjunction with the sun while in direct motion, then they separate from the sun until they become east of it, so they rise after it and set similarly, moving apart in this separation from it to some limit. So the farthest distance of Venus from the sun is 47 degrees, and the farthest distance of Mercury from it is 27 degrees. Then they return opposite to the (order of the) signs, approaching it until they fall into conjunction with it while retrograde, a second conjunction. Then they become western (i.e., they become west of it), so they set then before it, not after it, as he mentioned. And similarly they rise before it, moving apart in becoming west from it to some limit. Then they return from the direction of retrograde to the direction of direct motion until they approach it in direct motion, as we mentioned first. So it is known by that that the center of their epicycle in particular is attached to the center of the sun, and that their distance from it east or west is only due to the motion of their epicycle alone. As for the rest of the wandering planets, which are the upper ones, they are not like that; for their retrograde motion, rather its middle, occurs only when they are in opposition to the sun, so they are in the perigee then, just as the middle of their direct motion occurs only at the sun's conjunction with them, and they are then in the apogee.
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage is a detailed astronomical explanation of the motions of the five planets (the wandering planets) as observed from Earth. It begins by stating that these planets have an epicycle (تدوير) whose motion in its opposite half exceeds that of its carrier, as previously mentioned. Then it notes that the five planets appear to move among the fixed stars, overtaking them in conjunction and then leaving them behind to the west, from which it is deduced that the carrier of the epicycle moves from west to east (i.e., in the direction opposite to the daily rotation). This is a key proof for the existence of an epicycle carrier moving eastward. The passage then focuses on the two inferior planets, Venus and Mercury, describing their specific behavior relative to the sun. They are in conjunction with the sun while in direct motion, then separate eastward, rising and setting after the sun, with maximum angular distances of 47° for Venus and 27° for Mercury. Then they return retrograde (against the order of signs) toward the sun, meeting it in a second conjunction. After that, they become west of the sun, setting before it, and then rise before it while moving apart westward. Then they return to direct motion and approach the sun again. From this behavior, the author concludes that the center of their epicycle is fixed to the center of the sun, meaning their epicycle center moves with the sun, and their distance east or west is only due to motion on the epicycle itself. Then the passage contrasts this with the outer planets (the upper wandering planets: Mars, Jupiter, Saturn). For them, the middle of retrograde motion occurs at opposition with the sun (i.e., when the planet is directly opposite the sun in the sky), and that is when they are at perigee (closest to Earth on the epicycle). Conversely, the middle of direct motion occurs at conjunction with the sun, when they are at apogee (farthest from Earth on the epicycle). This shows that the outer planets' epicycle centers are not attached to the sun; rather, their behavior is tied to the sun's position relative to the Earth. The argument thus uses observational data to infer the structure of the Ptolemaic model, specifically the eccentric epicycle model for each planet.

Misconception & Correction

Correction: Venus and Mercury have their epicycle center attached to the sun, while the outer planets do not; their retrograde motion occurs at opposition.

Key Takeaway
The epicycle center of Venus and Mercury is fixed to the sun, while outer planets' epicycle centers are not, as shown by their conjunction and opposition behaviors.

Inclination of the Apogee-Perigee Diameter of Venus and Mercury
The commentator explains the inclination of the apogee-perigee diameter and its effect on latitude.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the diameter through the apogee and perigee of the epicycles of Venus and Mercury inclines relative to the orbit and how this inclination allows for additional latitudes.

Core Idea
The apogee-perigee diameter of the epicycle inclines only at the midpoint between nodes, causing latitude variation.

This passage focuses on the diameter of the epicycle that passes through its apogee and perigee. It explains that this diameter coincides with the orbit of the epicycle center only at the midpoint between the two nodes, while at the nodes it is at extreme inclination. This inclination allows Venus to have a southern latitude and Mercury a northern latitude.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the technical terms like 'ذروة' (apogee) and 'حضيض' (perigee).
2
Identify the key claim
Identify the claim that the diameter sometimes coincides with the orbit and sometimes separates, and that coincidence only occurs at the midpoint between nodes.
This is the core of the passage.
3
Understand the consequence for latitudes
Reflect on why this inclination enables Venus to have a southern latitude and Mercury a northern latitude.
The passage states this directly.
